<div id="review_364873766" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364873766" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10697179-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549097p2/10697179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364873766?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/10697179-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444740998" href="/book/show/18718925-between-the-lines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364873766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9467177020270275234"><b>
  <a href='http://thatgirlbookworm.blogspot.ca/2015/11/book-review-42-between-lines-by-jodi.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>View this review on my blog: thatgirlbookworm</a>
</b><br/><br/>I have to say, my rating for this one surprised me. It's no secret that Jodi Picoult is one of, if not my favorite author. I now own 21 of her books and my collection is only growing from here. But this one was not cutting it for me. 60% through the book this was still only a 2.5/5 star book for me. But it got so much better near the end and improved and I really enjoyed it to the point where it became a 4 star book.<br/><br/>This book had a GREAT concept. </span>
  <span id="freeText9467177020270275234" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="http://thatgirlbookworm.blogspot.ca/2015/11/book-review-42-between-lines-by-jodi.html" rel="nofollow noopener">View this review on my blog: thatgirlbookworm</a>
</b><br /><br />I have to say, my rating for this one surprised me. It's no secret that Jodi Picoult is one of, if not my favorite author. I now own 21 of her books and my collection is only growing from here. But this one was not cutting it for me. 60% through the book this was still only a 2.5/5 star book for me. But it got so much better near the end and improved and I really enjoyed it to the point where it became a 4 star book.<br /><br />This book had a GREAT concept. It follows a character named Oliver and a character named Delilah. Delilah is reading a fairy tale book when one day the character inside her book reaches out to her for help. What we don't know is that characters in books have actual lives whey the book is closed and Oliver has spent his entire existence wanting to be outside the book. The novel follows them and also there are chapters of the actual fairy tale in the book (which were my favorite chapters)<br /><br />I will say, as much as I loved the plot, I DO think that this concept could have been done better by someone else. Jodi Picoult is mainly an adult fiction writer. That's not to say she can't write young adult/middle grade books, I mean I know her daughter worked with her, but I just don't think this is the genre I would tell her to stick with. There were a lot of really cheesy and unbelievable moments that I just felt like the book could have done without. As well, I realize fairy tales ALWAYS have insta love and this book is meant to be read like a fairy tale, but the insta love was just not well done in my opinion in this one.<br /><br />Oliver is a really great character. Actually Oliver's world inside the book with Frump and stuff were just the best parts. I loved all the characters. But Delilah was where the characters fell flat for me. She was really juvenile for a teenager. Just immature and young and extremely annoying. She gets mad at her mom because her mom is worried about her, but girl you're talking to a novel, of course she's going to worry. She also gets mad that other people can't hear Oliver but like again no one really expects a novel to talk to them so of course they can't hear him. She was just senseless for a character and I was never rooting for her. <br />Also the fact that she just dumps everyone in her life for a boy really disgusts me but that's just something that bothers me in general in life so I just gravitated towards anger when she did this.<br /><br />Overall enjoyable. Best book ever? Definitely not. But cute, fun and easy to read. I can definitely see the appeal for little kids (and adults) who like fairy tales and they'd probably really enjoy this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9467177020270275234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_367584360" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/367584360" />
    <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland"><img alt="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417030210p2/5749698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/367584360?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland">Kat (Lost in Neverland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=cute-as-a-kitten">cute-as-a-kitten</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=eh">eh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=cheesy-romance">cheesy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer367584360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3287027786035669707">Oh LAWD, was that cheesy.<br/>That was one of the most corny books I've ever read.<br/><br/>Excuse me, review to be written after I've stopped vomiting rainbows and sunshine. <br/><br/><br/>Oliver is a prince, trapped inside the same fairytale and desperate to get out. When Delilah picks up the book, she falls in love with the story...and with Oliver. She's also the only one who can hear him. <br/>The two try every way possible to get Oliver out of the fairytale, but nothing works. How can they be together when Oliver is only ink</span>
  <span id="freeText3287027786035669707" style="display:none">Oh LAWD, was that cheesy.<br>That was one of the most corny books I've ever read.<br><br>Excuse me, review to be written after I've stopped vomiting rainbows and sunshine. <br><br><br>Oliver is a prince, trapped inside the same fairytale and desperate to get out. When Delilah picks up the book, she falls in love with the story...and with Oliver. She's also the only one who can hear him. <br>The two try every way possible to get Oliver out of the fairytale, but nothing works. How can they be together when Oliver is only ink on a page? <br><br>I almost gave up this book several times. The fact that I had already read nearly half of it kept me reading, forcing myself to finish. <br><br>It was cute. I liked the idea that the characters from our stories live on in the book after we close it. Like they were actors in a big movie that they had to play over and over again. <br>But it also reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28194.Inkheart__Inkheart___1_" title="Inkheart (Inkheart, #1) by Cornelia Funke" rel="nofollow noopener">Inkheart</a>. <br><br>Inkheart is about book characters who come to life out of a book (called <i>Inkheart</i>, just like the title of the actual book) and a girl has to change the ending to save her family and herself. <br>Between the Lines is about book characters who come to life inside the book (called <i>Between the Lines</i>. Again, the same concept) and a girl has to change the ending to save Oliver.<br>(Okay, it's actually not Delilah, but I'm not gonna spoil that) <br><br>They're both completely different stories, but those similarities veer dangerously close to copycat material. <br><br>The writing wasn't great. It was elementary, at best. I mean, <u>I</u> can write better than this. <br><br>The 'love' between Oliver and Delilah was kind of...weird. I don't know, maybe because for most of the book he was the size of half a page. <br><br>I was a little pissed off about the ending. I didn't notice it when I finished at first, but after I thought about it, it miffed me a bit. <br><br><br>But I won't get into that because I don't wanna spoil anything for those who still want to read it themselves and make their own assumption.<br><br>If I could summarize this book in three words, they'd be;<br><br>1. Cute<br>2. Corny<br>3. A little bit Copycat<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383849ra/742254.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3287027786035669707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('T2qMz/UFqT6r2AwGeoN79CCqxBPNLUGHGihm+5LH7KXMjsXXbxFriRFwYQlnvv4n7nKjzjkbkOYvvA0jF0kHnw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YjhJmzWPGWNaQmHM0d+WsK3xo34HqdgunxQFbSaoWOPh3ACDr5vb1ODqDMPM4hNjYynEo/OfCU+qgG61oyaz2Q==')})
  }
